<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Babymetal</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><b>Babymetal</b> (stylized as <b>BABYMETAL</b>) is a Japanese <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">metal</a> <a href="/wiki/Japanese_idol" title="Japanese idol">idol</a> band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Their line-up consists of <a href="/wiki/Suzuka_Nakamoto" title="Suzuka Nakamoto">Suzuka Nakamoto</a> as "Su-metal", <a href="/wiki/Yui_Mizuno" title="Yui Mizuno">Yui Mizuno</a> as "Yuimetal", and <a href="/wiki/Moa_Kikuchi" title="Moa Kikuchi">Moa Kikuchi</a> as "Moametal". The concept of the group is a fusion of the heavy metal and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_idol" title="Japanese idol">Japanese idol</a> genres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oricon20130121_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-oricon20130121-10">[10]</a></sup> The three teenage girls and their band are managed by the <a href="/wiki/Amuse,_Inc." title="Amuse, Inc.">Amuse talent agency</a>. Their vocals are backed by heavy metal instrumentation played by the Kami Band. Babymetal released their <a href="/wiki/Babymetal_(album)" title="Babymetal (album)">eponymous debut album</a> in February 2014. Their second album <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Resistance" title="Metal Resistance">Metal Resistance</a></i> was released worldwide on April 1, 2016<span style="display:none"> (<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2016-04-01</span>)</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babymetal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010.E2.80.932012:_Beginnings">2010–2012: Beginnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babymetal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 2010–2012: Beginnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The group was initially formed in 2010 as a subunit of the female <a href="/wiki/Japanese_idol" title="Japanese idol">idol</a> group <a href="/wiki/Sakura_Gakuin" title="Sakura Gakuin">Sakura Gakuin</a>, aiming to realize a "fusion of metal and idol [music]".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barks-biography_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-barks-biography-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV_Iggy_report_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_Iggy_report-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jcast201112-16116731_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-jcast201112-16116731-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kawaiigirljapan20120214_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-kawaiigirljapan20120214-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> None of the three members knew what metal music was before the inception of the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-razortv684979_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-razortv684979-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Babymetal's first live appearance was on 28 November 2010, at Sakura Gakuin's first solo concert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hmv20121228_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-hmv20121228-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Their first song, "<a href="/wiki/Doki_Doki_Morning" title="Doki Doki Morning">Doki Doki Morning</a>", was originally released in April 2011 on the Sakura Gakuin album <i>Sakura Gakuin 2010 Nendo: Message</i>. The band shot a music video for the song and in October 2011 released it as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DVD_single" title="DVD single">DVD single</a> intended for limited (live-venues-only) distribution. Having been uploaded to YouTube that same month, by the end of 2012 the video totaled over 1 million views.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barks-biography_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-barks-biography-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jcast201112-16116731_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-jcast201112-16116731-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hmv20121228_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-hmv20121228-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sozo20131207_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-sozo20131207-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rocketnews24_interview_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rocketnews24_interview-22">[22]</a></sup> In July 2011, Babymetal premiered the song, "<a href="/wiki/Ijime,_Dame,_Zettai" title="Ijime, Dame, Zettai">Ijime, Dame, Zettai</a>" ("No More Bullying"), at a Sakura Gakuin concert, but it would only be performed during live concerts at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV_Iggy_report_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_Iggy_report-13">[13]</a></sup> The first music video, "Doki Doki Morning" was released from the <a href="/wiki/Toy%27s_Factory" title="Toy's Factory">Toy's Factory</a> channel on YouTube at 12 October 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Babymetal's first CD single was a collaboration with the band Kiba of Akiba, titled "<a href="/wiki/Babymetal_%C3%97_Kiba_of_Akiba" title="Babymetal × Kiba of Akiba">Babymetal × Kiba of Akiba</a>". Released on a sublabel of Toy's Factory (Jūonbu Records, same sublabel as "Doki Doki Morning" and later "Headbanger") in March 2012,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sakuragakuin-news20120209_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-sakuragakuin-news20120209-4">[4]</a></sup> it ranked 3rd on the <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> weekly indie chart and number one in the <a href="/wiki/Tower_Records#Japan" title="Tower Records">Tower Records Shibuya</a> weekly indie ranking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deview20120427_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-deview20120427-24">[24]</a></sup> In July 2012, Babymetal released a single titled "<a href="/wiki/Headbanger_(Babymetal_song)" title="Headbanger (Babymetal song)">Headbanger</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deview20120427_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-deview20120427-24">[24]</a></sup> The music video for the title track was directed by Hidenobu Tanabe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-headbangya-director_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-headbangya-director-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In August 2012, Babymetal debuted at Japan's <a href="/wiki/Summer_Sonic_Festival" title="Summer Sonic Festival">Summer Sonic Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hmv20121228_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-hmv20121228-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-musicman-net20120820_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-musicman-net20120820-27">[27]</a></sup> With the average age of 12, the band became the youngest act ever to perform there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sozo20131207_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-sozo20131207-21">[21]</a></sup> 2012 also marks Babymetal first Asian tour outside of Japan for the very first time at AFA 2012 Singapore<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013.E2.80.932015:_Major_label_debut">2013–2015: Major label debut</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babymetal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2013–2015: Major label debut">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2013, the band debuted on a major record label with "<a href="/wiki/Ijime,_Dame,_Zettai" title="Ijime, Dame, Zettai">Ijime, Dame, Zettai</a>". It sold 19,000 copies in its first week and debuted at number 6 in the <a href="/wiki/Oricon_Singles_Chart" title="Oricon Singles Chart">Oricon Weekly Singles Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oricon20130121_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-oricon20130121-10">[10]</a></sup> In the spring of 2013, Nakamoto graduated from junior high school and therefore had to "graduate" from Sakura Gakuin (a group of elementary and junior high school girls). However, their management decided that Babymetal would not dissolve and would continue its activities as a band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kawaiigirljapan20120214_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-kawaiigirljapan20120214-15">[15]</a></sup> The group released its next single, "<a href="/wiki/Megitsune" title="Megitsune">Megitsune</a>", on June 19,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-japanverse20130416_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-japanverse20130416-29">[29]</a></sup> followed in November by the live video release <i><a href="/wiki/Live:_Legend_I,_D,_Z_Apocalypse" title="Live: Legend I, D, Z Apocalypse">Live: Legend I, D, Z Apocalypse</a></i>, which debuted at seventh place in the weekly Oricon Blu-ray Disc charts, and at the second place among music Blu-rays.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oricon20131127_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-oricon20131127-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 and 11 August 2013, Babymetal again took part in the Summer Sonic Festival, performing both in Tokyo and Osaka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Later, in October 2013, Babymetal also became the youngest act ever to perform at the heavy metal music festival <a href="/wiki/Loud_Park_Festival" title="Loud Park Festival">Loud Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sozo20131207_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-sozo20131207-21">[21]</a></sup> In November 2013, Babymetal released a promo video for the Japanese premiere of <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a>'s movie <i><a href="/wiki/Metallica_Through_the_Never" title="Metallica Through the Never">Through the Never</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baby_Metal_advertise_Metallica_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Baby_Metal_advertise_Metallica-32">[32]</a></sup> And near at the end of 2013 Babymetal did another Asian tour in Indonesia at AFAID 2013<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> and second time for SIngapore after their first overseas Asian tour in 2012.</p>
<p>On 26 February 2014, Babymetal released its first, <a href="/wiki/Babymetal_(album)" title="Babymetal (album)">self-titled album</a>. It contained thirteen tracks and was also available in a limited edition that included a DVD with music videos and live footage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-albumnews_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-albumnews-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2dayconcert_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-2dayconcert-35">[35]</a></sup> The album was very well received by music critics<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone-review_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-review-36">[36]</a></sup> as well as the public, selling over 37,000 copies in Japan its first week, debuting at number four in Oricon<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> and number 2 in <i>Billboard Japan</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BillboardJapan20140310_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-BillboardJapan20140310-38">[38]</a></sup> It also topped <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">Metal</a> charts in Germany, UK and US, and reached number 187 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart on March 22; few Japanese artists have ever entered the chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bb200_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-bb200-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Their album also made it into the <a href="/wiki/Top_Heatseekers" title="Top Heatseekers">Heatseekers</a> chart at number four.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> On March 1 and 2, 2014, the band gave two concerts at <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Budokan" title="Nippon Budokan">Budokan</a>. With the average age of 14.7, they became youngest-ever female act to give a show there. The two concerts were attended by 20,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> On 3 April 2014, the reaction video by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/YouTubers" title="YouTubers">YouTubers</a> with shock was released from the <a href="/wiki/Fine_Brothers" title="Fine Brothers">Fine Brothers</a> channel on YouTube about the Music Videos of "<a href="/wiki/Doki_Doki_Morning" title="Doki Doki Morning">Doki Doki Morning</a>", "line!",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> and "<a href="/wiki/Gimme_Chocolate!!" title="Gimme Chocolate!!">Gimme Chocolate!!</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youtuber2014a_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-youtuber2014a-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youtuber2014b_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-youtuber2014b-46">[46]</a></sup> On 30 April 2016, the video of Babymetal's reaction to their reaction was released on YouTube.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youtuber2016_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-youtuber2016-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, Babymetal performed in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, and in the UK at the <a href="/wiki/Sonisphere_Festival#Sonisphere_2014" title="Sonisphere Festival">Sonisphere Festival 2014</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> They made their debut appearance in the US on July 27 with a headlining show at <a href="/wiki/The_Fonda_Theatre" title="The Fonda Theatre">The Fonda Theatre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> They played <a href="/wiki/Heavy_MONTR%C3%89AL" title="Heavy MONTRÉAL">Heavy MONTRÉAL</a> 2014 in Canada on August 9 alongside <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slayer" title="Slayer">Slayer</a>, and also performed at Summer Sonic 2014 in Japan on the Mountain Stage with bands such as <a href="/wiki/Avenged_Sevenfold" title="Avenged Sevenfold">Avenged Sevenfold</a> and <a href="/wiki/Megadeth" title="Megadeth">Megadeth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-babymetal.jp-about_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-babymetal.jp-about-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Babymetal was also the opening act to five of <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>'s concerts in her "<a href="/wiki/ArtRave:_The_Artpop_Ball" title="ArtRave: The Artpop Ball">ArtRave: The Artpop Ball</a>" 2014 tour in August along the western United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2014, it was announced that the band would be returning to England to play another show at <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/O2_Academy_Brixton" title="O2 Academy Brixton">O2 Academy Brixton</a> on November 8,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-London_November_8_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-London_November_8-54">[54]</a></sup> their final European show of the year as part of the group's "Babymetal Apocalypse" phase. It was later announced that the band would also be returning to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, which they had visited earlier in the year without giving an actual performance, performing in the <a href="/wiki/Hammerstein_Ballroom" title="Hammerstein Ballroom">Hammerstein Ballroom</a> on November 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In September the band announced their second live album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Live:_Legend_1999_%26_1997_Apocalypse" title="Live: Legend 1999 &amp; 1997 Apocalypse">Live: Legend 1999 &amp; 1997 Apocalypse</a></i>, released on October 19 on <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a> and <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a>, featuring their live performances at both the <a href="/wiki/NHK_Hall" title="NHK Hall">NHK Hall</a> and at <a href="/wiki/Makuhari_Messe" title="Makuhari Messe">Makuhari Messe</a> Event Hall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-second_live_dvd_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-second_live_dvd-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>At their Brixton performance, the band debuted a new song titled "<a href="/wiki/Road_of_Resistance" title="Road of Resistance">Road of Resistance</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blabberRoR_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-blabberRoR-57">[57]</a></sup> It was later revealed to be a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Sam_Totman" title="Sam Totman">Sam Totman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Herman_Li" title="Herman Li">Herman Li</a> of prominent <a href="/wiki/Power_metal" title="Power metal">power metal</a> band <a href="/wiki/DragonForce" title="DragonForce">DragonForce</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blabberRoR_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-blabberRoR-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The song, featuring Li and Totman on guitars, was subsequently released as a bonus track available with the "Red Night" edition of their "Live at Budokan" album on January 7, 2015, and as part of the exclusive Fan Club "The One" edition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-budokan-lors_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-budokan-lors-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-budokan-bmnet_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-budokan-bmnet-60">[60]</a></sup> Li later revealed via Twitter and Facebook posts that he and Totman had been working on the song's guitar parts since 2013. Shortly after the joint release with <i><a href="/wiki/Live_at_Budokan:_Red_Night" title="Live at Budokan: Red Night">Live at Budokan: Red Night</a></i>, it was released as a single on the iTunes store. In April 2015, the band announced the re-release of their self-titled album via <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EarMUSIC" title="EarMUSIC">earMUSIC</a> in the UK on June 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Ahead of their performance at the <a href="/wiki/Metal_Hammer" title="Metal Hammer">Metal Hammer</a> Golden Gods Awards on June 15, the trio made a surprise appearance during <a href="/wiki/DragonForce" title="DragonForce">DragonForce</a>'s set at <a href="/wiki/Download_Festival" title="Download Festival">Download Festival</a>, performing "<a href="/wiki/Gimme_Chocolate!!" title="Gimme Chocolate!!">Gimme Chocolate!!</a>", despite event organizer Andy Copping stating that he would never book the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016.E2.80.93present:_Touring_and_Metal_Resistance">2016–present: Touring and <i>Metal Resistance</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babymetal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2016–present: Touring and Metal Resistance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Babymetal_performing_at_Wembley_Arena,_London_(26201667231).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Babymetal_performing_at_Wembley_Arena%2C_London_%2826201667231%29.jpg/220px-Babymetal_performing_at_Wembley_Arena%2C_London_%2826201667231%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Babymetal_performing_at_Wembley_Arena%2C_London_%2826201667231%29.jpg/330px-Babymetal_performing_at_Wembley_Arena%2C_London_%2826201667231%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Babymetal_performing_at_Wembley_Arena%2C_London_%2826201667231%29.jpg/440px-Babymetal_performing_at_Wembley_Arena%2C_London_%2826201667231%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Babymetal_performing_at_Wembley_Arena,_London_(26201667231).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Babymetal performing at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Arena" title="Wembley Arena">Wembley Arena</a>, 2016.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the band's 2-day concerts in <a href="/wiki/Yokohama" title="Yokohama">Yokohama</a> in December 2015, it was announced that they would be releasing a <a href="/wiki/Metal_Resistance" title="Metal Resistance">second studio album</a> on April 1, 2016, as well as a new world tour starting in London at the <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Arena" title="Wembley Arena">Wembley Arena</a>, and concluding in Japan with the band's debut performance in the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Dome" title="Tokyo Dome">Tokyo Dome</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ro69151214_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-ro69151214-63">[63]</a></sup> On January 15, 2016, the second album's title was revealed to be <i>Metal Resistance</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> On April 2, one day after the release of <i>Metal Resistance</i>, Babymetal became the first Japanese act to headline Wembley Arena,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> with the largest sale of merchandise for a single day event in the venue's history,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Babymetal_break_2_UK_records_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Babymetal_break_2_UK_records-66">[66]</a></sup> coinciding with the highest ever entry for an album in the UK charts for a Japanese act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Babymetal_break_2_UK_records_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-Babymetal_break_2_UK_records-66">[66]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> gave their Wembley performance a rating of five out of five stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> On April 5, Babymetal made their U.S. television debut, performing "<a href="/wiki/Gimme_Chocolate!!" title="Gimme Chocolate!!">Gimme Chocolate!!</a>" on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Late_Show_with_Stephen_Colbert" title="The Late Show with Stephen Colbert">The Late Show with Stephen Colbert</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Babymetal were added as a character skin in the <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a> video game <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Mario_Maker" title="Super Mario Maker">Super Mario Maker</a></i> in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 26, 2016, it was announced by <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWE</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Triple_H" title="Triple H">Triple H</a> on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> that their song "<a href="/wiki/Karate_(song)" title="Karate (song)">Karate</a>", along with <a href="/wiki/A_Day_to_Remember" title="A Day to Remember">A Day to Remember</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Paranoia_(A_Day_to_Remember_song)" title="Paranoia (A Day to Remember song)">Paranoia</a>", would be used as one of the official theme songs of <a href="/wiki/NXT_TakeOver:_The_End" title="NXT TakeOver: The End">NXT TakeOver: The End</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 18, the band made a special appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Alternative_Press_Music_Awards" title="Alternative Press Music Awards">Alternative Press Music Awards</a> where they performed "Karate" before being joined onstage by <a href="/wiki/Judas_Priest" title="Judas Priest">Judas Priest</a> frontman <a href="/wiki/Rob_Halford" title="Rob Halford">Rob Halford</a>. Halford, along with Nakamoto and the Kami Band, performed an abridged version of "<a href="/wiki/Painkiller_(Judas_Priest_song)" title="Painkiller (Judas Priest song)">Painkiller</a>", followed by a performance of "<a href="/wiki/Breaking_the_Law" title="Breaking the Law">Breaking the Law</a>" where they were rejoined by Mizuno and Kikuchi on guitars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 27, <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Hammer" title="Metal Hammer">Metal Hammer</a></i> readers voted Babymetal's <a href="/wiki/Babymetal_(album)" title="Babymetal (album)">debut album</a> as the best album of the 21st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2016, <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> announced that a hybrid live action-animation fantasy-adventure short form series featuring the members of the band was under development. The series would be developed by Blue Ribbon Content in collaboration with Amuse Group USA (an Amuse Inc. subsidiary based in the United States). The band's producer, Kobametal, is also involved with production of the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 19 (Red Night) and September 20 2016 (Black Night), Babymetal ended their Babymetal World Tour 2016: Legend - Metal Resistance by performing at the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Dome" title="Tokyo Dome">Tokyo Dome</a>. Both nights were sold out. The attendance for each night was approximately 55,000 people. These included fans from <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and many others from around the world. Yuimetal admits she is "still in shock" that she's playing here (Tokyo Dome). Moametal feels the same, admitting it is "definitely a big challenge for young girls of our age to stand on that stage". Su-metal explained that "In Japan we have played many big venues like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Budokan" title="Budokan">Budokan</a> and others, but <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Dome" title="Tokyo Dome">Tokyo Dome</a> was always a place that I have been dreaming of performing at."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2016, Babymetal supported the <a href="/wiki/Red_Hot_Chili_Peppers" title="Red Hot Chili Peppers">Red Hot Chili Peppers</a> during <a href="/wiki/The_Getaway_World_Tour" title="The Getaway World Tour">The Getaway World Tour</a> in the UK. During their final show on the tour, Red Hot Chili Peppers drummer <a href="/wiki/Chad_Smith" title="Chad Smith">Chad Smith</a> joined Babymetal onstage to perform their covers of Judas Priest's "Painkiller" and "Breaking the Law". After the performance, Smith thanked Babymetal for being on tour with them and led the audience in singing "Happy Birthday" to Su-metal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2017, Babymetal supported <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a> for their <a href="/wiki/WorldWired_Tour" title="WorldWired Tour">WorldWired Tour</a> at <a href="/wiki/Gocheok_Sky_Dome" title="Gocheok Sky Dome">Gocheok Sky Dome</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> and will also appear in Japan's performance of the <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N' Roses">Guns N' Roses</a>' <a href="/wiki/Not_in_This_Lifetime..._Tour" title="Not in This Lifetime... Tour">Not in This Lifetime... Tour</a> as the opening act.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style_and_lyrics">Musical style and lyrics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babymetal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Musical style and lyrics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The band defines its style as a new genre called "<a href="/wiki/Kawaii_metal" title="Kawaii metal">kawaii metal</a>" ("<a href="/wiki/Kawaii" title="Kawaii">kawaii</a>" meaning "cute") and clarifies that it is "a mix of <a href="/wiki/J-pop" title="J-pop">J-pop</a> idol and heavy metal"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barks-biography_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-barks-biography-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-babymetal.jp-about_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-babymetal.jp-about-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Huffington_Post_comment_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Huffington_Post_comment-79">[79]</a></sup> In the music press, the group is most commonly associated with the genres <a href="/wiki/Death_metal" title="Death metal">death metal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Speed_metal" title="Speed metal">speed metal</a> and <a href="/wiki/J-pop" title="J-pop">J-pop</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV_Iggy_report_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_Iggy_report-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rock_In_Japan_2013_interview_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rock_In_Japan_2013_interview-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tristan Peterson, of Metal Obsession, remarked in his review of the band's debut album "This band was created for the demographic of “Music that your Japanese Boyfriend/Girlfriend, who doesn’t really like Metal, would enjoy.” as well as "[Babymetal] has made metal cute without losing any of its edge." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>Patrick St. Michel from Japanese music and culture site <i>MTV 81</i> praises the "pure, headbang-inducing energy" of the group's live performances and describes their style as a mixture of "...seemingly disparate sounds of heavy metal and idol pop, creating music anchored both by throat-mauling screeches and cuddly choruses."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Hammer" title="Metal Hammer">Metal Hammer</a></i> described their act using the formula "Short skirts, school girl charm and squeaky voices — just like in the manga comics. But they mix the whole thing with Metal.".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metalhammer_description_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Metalhammer_description-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lyrical themes found in Babymetal's music focus on real-world issues and also typical idol-pop topics such as encouraging young teens to accept and stand up for themselves, the pressure put on teenage girls to remain thin and also bullying while they also sing about what it's like going to your first concert, the concept of an "ideal woman" and chocolate, subjects which critics say are a step away from typical lyrical styles used by most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metal_music" title="Metal music">metal</a> bands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Babymetal_Japan_Times_review_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Babymetal_Japan_Times_review-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_performances">Live performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babymetal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Live performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Besides dancing, the trio all perform vocals. Su-metal is the main vocalist, credited on Babymetal's official site with vocals and dancing, while Moametal and Yuimetal are credited with scream and dance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rocketnews24_interview_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rocketnews24_interview-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-babymetal.jp-about_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-babymetal.jp-about-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phoenix_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-phoenix-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Babymetal's costumes take a variety of cues from the popular Japanese Gothic and Punk Lolita styles, with an emphasis on red and black.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jcast201112-16116731_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-jcast201112-16116731-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barks20120621_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-barks20120621-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Instead of the <a href="/wiki/Sign_of_the_horns" title="Sign of the horns">sign of the horns</a>, the band uses the hand gesture of the <a href="/wiki/Kitsune" title="Kitsune">kitsune</a> to symbolise the band's supposed divine inspiration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rocketnews24_interview_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rocketnews24_interview-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>In their concerts, Babymetal are accompanied by a <a href="/wiki/Backup_band" title="Backup band">backing band</a>. In their early stages, the backing band consisted of the "Babybones" - a group of nameless individuals dressed in skeleton costumes that would mimick live performances while pre-recorded studio tracks were being used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barks-kawaiigirljapan20131004_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-barks-kawaiigirljapan20131004-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barks20131121_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-barks20131121-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> In late 2012, Babymetal debuted a live band for their live performances which they referred to as "Full Metal Band" - a group of live musicians dressed in white robes and <a href="/wiki/Corpse_paint" title="Corpse paint">corpse paint</a>. They have since been referred to by band members and fans as "Gods of Metal" and more recently "Kami Band". From late 2012 to early 2014, the two groups would alternate, with the Kami Band being used more for festival appearances and special events. As of early 2014, the Babybones band has been quietly retired, and the Kami Band has since been established as Babymetal's primary backing band.</p>
<p>The Kami Band has consisted of a rotating line-up of different musicians since its debut in late 2012. As of late 2013, however, the line-up has been relatively stable, consisting of guitarists Takayoshi Ohmura, Leda, Mikio Fujioka, and Isao, bassist Boh, and drummers Hideki Aoyama and Yuya Maeta with members occasionally substituting for one another if needed. Kami Band member Leda has contributed to Babymetal's music, most notably on their album <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Resistance" title="Metal Resistance">Metal Resistance</a></i> (credited as Ledametal).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_image">Public image</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babymetal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Public image">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to Kei "Kobametal" Kobayashi, the band's executive producer, the band was formed under the idea of a new type of metal, and the members of the band receive "divine messages" from the Fox God, though Nakamoto explained that the messages received were indirect, as they would be sent to Kobametal first.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nylon_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-nylon-94">[94]</a></sup> He stated that it was up to the people's decision to accept or reject the idea. Additionally, he rejected the notion of the band being a "metal" or "pop" act, preferring "the one and only Babymetal."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Kikuchi joked that the three members did not decide to join the band, as it was a destiny chosen by the Fox God, whose goal is said to have the band perform and spread their music all over the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-admit_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-admit-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The band has received varied reception by the public. Some critics praised the band for being "creative" and "rule-breaking" in the metal genre,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theguardian-review_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian-review-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cosreview_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-cosreview-98">[98]</a></sup> while others called the band a "novelty group" and a "silly balancing act".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nmereview_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-nmereview-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusicreview_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicreview-100">[100]</a></sup> When asked about people who do not consider the band's pop-infused music "metal", Nakamoto acknowledged the claims and praised such accusations, warranting how metal "purists" have their own preferences for metal being a certain way, and taking them into consideration for the band's progress. Additionally, the band members believe in staying true to themselves and enjoying what they do, as she agrees is enough for them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-admit_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-admit-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The fanbase, collectively referred to as "The One",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nylon_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-nylon-94">[94]</a></sup> has been noted by Mizuno to be a mixed demographic of varying age. Noting the fans of metal and pop, she described the "metalheads" who look like themselves, and the pop fans who dress and cosplay as them. She hopes to be able to continue to reach out to all different types of people. When asked about being role models for their fans and young girls, considered it an honor. She further emphasized the importance of being able to reach out to the youth, especially for younger music fans branching out to the metal genre via Babymetal, noting her own lack of experience of metal before joining the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-admit_96-2"><a href="#cite_note-admit-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Members">Members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babymetal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Babymetal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-count references-column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2; list-style-type: upper-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-129"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-129">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Released as a DVD single.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-131"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-131">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Charted at number 50 on the <i>Billboard Japan</i> Hot Singles Sales chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-133"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-133">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Charted at number 19 on the <i>Billboard Japan</i> Hot Singles Sales chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-135"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-135">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Released exclusively in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[131]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-138"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-138">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Also known as Kamiguchi <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">かみぐち</span><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>. The music videos he directed include "<a href="/wiki/Crazy_Kanzen_na_Otona" title="Crazy Kanzen na Otona">Crazy Kanzen na Otona</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Kanashiki_Amefuri_/_Adam_to_Eve_no_Dilemma" title="Kanashiki Amefuri / Adam to Eve no Dilemma">Kanashiki Amefuri</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Kanashiki_Amefuri_/_Adam_to_Eve_no_Dilemma" title="Kanashiki Amefuri / Adam to Eve no Dilemma">Adam to Even no Dilemma</a>" by the girl group <a href="/wiki/Cute_(Japanese_idol_group)" title="Cute (Japanese idol group)">Cute</a>.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
